</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://comptongame.com">comptongame<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Jayceon Terrell Taylor</b> (born November 29, 1979), better known by his stage name <b>the Game</b> or simply <b>Game</b>, is an American rapper. Born in <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a>, he initially released a series of <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a> under the wing of fellow West Coast rapper <a href="/wiki/JT_the_Bigga_Figga" title="JT the Bigga Figga">JT the Bigga Figga</a>. After releasing his debut independent album <i><a href="/wiki/Untold_Story_(album)" title="Untold Story (album)">Untold Story</a></i> in 2004, he was eventually discovered by record producer <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> and signed to his <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Aftermath Records">Aftermath Records</a> label imprint. The Game rose to fame in 2005 with the success of his major-label debut album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Documentary" title="The Documentary">The Documentary</a></i> and found continued success with the 2006 follow-up <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor%27s_Advocate" title="Doctor&#39;s Advocate">Doctor's Advocate</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> certified <i>The Documentary</i> Double Platinum in March 2005.
</p><p>A rising artist in the 2000s, the Game was considered to be a driving force in bringing back the West Coast hip hop scene into the mainstream and competing with many of his <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_hip_hop" title="East Coast hip hop">East Coast counterparts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The Game was placed into <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a> by Dr. Dre and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>. As a result of his disputes with <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, Game left Aftermath and signed with <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen</a>, another label under <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Geffen_A%26M" class="mw-redirect" title="Interscope Geffen A&amp;M">Interscope Geffen A&amp;M</a> unit, to terminate his contractual obligations with G-Unit in the summer of 2006. The Game's second major label album <i>Doctor's Advocate</i> was released on November 14, 2006, and it became his second album to debut at number one on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart. <i>Doctor's Advocate</i> did not feature any production from Dr. Dre. <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" class="mw-redirect" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a> placed <i>The Documentary</i> at number 35 on their list of Top 50 Albums of 2005. The Game was nominated with a total of two nominations, including Grammy Award for Best Rap Song and Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance by a Duo or Group for the smash single "<a href="/wiki/Hate_It_or_Love_It" title="Hate It or Love It">Hate It or Love It</a>". <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> named <i>Doctor's Advocate</i> best hip-hop album of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His next album <i><a href="/wiki/LAX_(album)" title="LAX (album)">LAX</a></i> was released in 2008. With his fourth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_R.E.D._Album" title="The R.E.D. Album">The R.E.D. Album</a></i>, the Game again debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200. In addition to music, the Game has starred in motion pictures and founded <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Wall_Street_Records" title="The Black Wall Street Records">The Black Wall Street Records</a>. In September 2011, the Game started working on his fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Piece_(album)" title="Jesus Piece (album)">Jesus Piece</a></i>, which was released on December 11, 2012, his final album released by Interscope. In 2015, the Game released two albums, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Documentary_2" title="The Documentary 2">The Documentary 2</a></i> on October 9, and a week later on October 16, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Documentary_2.5" title="The Documentary 2.5">The Documentary 2.5</a></i>. His next album <i><a href="/wiki/1992_(album)" title="1992 (album)">1992</a></i> was released on October 14, 2016, and spawned two official singles. In 2019 he released <i><a href="/wiki/Born_2_Rap" title="Born 2 Rap">Born 2 Rap</a></i>, which he announced to be his final studio album; however, it was announced that in 2022 his career would continue with the release of his tenth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Drillmatic_%E2%80%93_Heart_vs._Mind" title="Drillmatic – Heart vs. Mind">Drillmatic – Heart vs. Mind</a></i>  .<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>The Game was born Jayceon Terrell Taylor<sup id="cite_ref-About_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> on November 29, 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-askmen_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-askmen-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> to parents George Taylor<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and Lynette Baker,<sup id="cite_ref-billboard-tardio_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-tardio-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> who both were members of the <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">Crips</a> street gang. He grew up in a primarily <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">Crip</a>-controlled neighborhood known as Santana Blocc,<sup id="cite_ref-askmen_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-askmen-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> although Taylor himself grew up to become a member of the <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Block_Piru" title="Cedar Block Piru">Cedar Block Piru Bloods</a> through his brother.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In an October 2006 interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> correspondent <a href="/wiki/Sway_Calloway" title="Sway Calloway">Sway Calloway</a>, the Game described his family as "<a href="/wiki/Dysfunctional_family" title="Dysfunctional family">dysfunctional</a>". His older half-brother, George Taylor III, a.k.a. the rapper <a href="/wiki/Big_Fase_100" title="Big Fase 100">Big Fase 100</a>, was a Cedar Block Piru Bloods leader in <a href="/wiki/West_Compton,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="West Compton, California">West Compton, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAWeekly-Weiss_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAWeekly-Weiss-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Taylor and his sibling spent six years in <a href="/wiki/Foster_care" title="Foster care">foster care</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard-tardio_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-tardio-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Taylor attended <a href="/wiki/Compton_High_School" title="Compton High School">Compton High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chicagotribune-hilburn_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune-hilburn-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He went on to attend the community colleges <a href="/wiki/Antelope_Valley_College" title="Antelope Valley College">Antelope Valley College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harbor_Community_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbor Community College">Harbor Community College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cerritos_College" title="Cerritos College">Cerritos College</a> each for a time before leaving school.<sup id="cite_ref-LAWeekly-Weiss_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAWeekly-Weiss-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the early 2000s, Taylor had become heavily involved in selling drugs and participating in gang activities.<sup id="cite_ref-EarlyLife_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EarlyLife-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career">Music career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Early_career_.282002.E2.80.932003.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_(2002–2003)">Early career (2002–2003)</span></h3>
<p>While recovering in the hospital from gunshot wounds he incurred in late 2001, Game told his brother to go out and buy all of the classic hip-hop albums. Over the course of five months, he studied all of the various influential rap albums and developed a strategy to turn himself into a rapper. With the help of his older brother <a href="/wiki/Big_Fase" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Fase">Big Fase</a>, they founded the label. It originally featured such artists as <a href="/wiki/Glasses_Malone" title="Glasses Malone">Glasses Malone</a>, Vita, and Nu Jerzey Devil, along with Game himself.<sup id="cite_ref-Shadows_3_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shadows_3-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Stage_name" title="Stage name">stage name</a> was coined by his grandmother, who was a huge fan of the 1997 blockbuster, <a href="/wiki/The_Game_(1997_film)" title="The Game (1997 film)"><i>The Game</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shadows_3_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shadows_3-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Game first gained prominence when he attended a hip-hop summit hosted by <a href="/wiki/Russell_Simmons" title="Russell Simmons">Russell Simmons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan" title="Louis Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> After he had fully recovered, Game and Big Fase made a mixtape together. He released his first mixtape <i>You Know What It Is Vol. 1</i> in 2002, and landed a record deal with the independent label <a href="/wiki/Get_Low_Recordz" title="Get Low Recordz">Get Low Recordz</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/JT_the_Bigga_Figga" title="JT the Bigga Figga">JT the Bigga Figga</a>.
</p><p>Game's mixtape reached the hands of <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean Combs</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_Records" title="Bad Boy Records">Bad Boy Records</a>, who originally was on the verge of signing him to his label.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Five months later, he was discovered by <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> who listened to the mixtape that had been produced by his brother. Dr. Dre contacted Game and signed him to his <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> label in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-observer_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observer-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In late 2003, <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a> and Dr. Dre decided to have Game work with <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a> in order to help build a growing buzz around Game which would also fuel interest in G-Unit. Game made his first cameo appearance in the music video for 50 Cent's "<a href="/wiki/In_da_Club" title="In da Club">In da Club</a>", where he is seen dancing with a girl. Since then, he has made numerous cameo appearances in music videos by 50 Cent, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Buck" title="Young Buck">Young Buck</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fabolous" title="Fabolous">Fabolous</a>. Game spent the next two and a half years working on his major label debut album and being mentored by Dr. Dre.<sup id="cite_ref-Shadows_3_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shadows_3-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="The_Documentary_.282003.E2.80.932005.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Documentary_(2003–2005)"><i>The Documentary</i> (2003–2005)</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg/220px-Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg/330px-Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg/440px-Kool_G_Rap_%26_The_Game.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>Game (right) with <a href="/wiki/Kool_G_Rap" title="Kool G Rap">Kool G Rap</a> (left) in New York City, November 2004</figcaption></figure>
<p>Not having dropped an album despite being signed onto Aftermath Entertainment and Interscope Records for a while, Game was still able to create hype around his image alone. He appeared in ads for <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean Combs</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sean_John" title="Sean John">Sean John</a> clothing company and had an endorsement deal with <a href="/wiki/Boost_Mobile_(United_States)" title="Boost Mobile (United States)">Boost Mobile</a>, appearing in a commercial alongside <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>. Game also appeared heavily on the mixtape circuit and guest starred on mixtapes for <a href="/wiki/DJ_Green_Lantern" title="DJ Green Lantern">DJ Green Lantern</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Diplomats" title="The Diplomats">The Diplomats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>. The first single released with Game on it was "<a href="/wiki/Certified_Gangstas" title="Certified Gangstas">Certified Gangstas</a>", which also featured <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones_(rapper)" title="Jim Jones (rapper)">Jim Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cam%27ron" title="Cam&#39;ron">Cam'ron</a>. Though the single wasn't considered to be mainstream, the buzz increased around the West Coast rapper.
</p><p>On September 28, 2004, Game released his first promo single, "<a href="/wiki/Westside_Story_(song)" title="Westside Story (song)">Westside Story</a>", from his major label debut album. He had originally chosen to title the album <i>Nigga Wit' An Attitude Volume 1</i> (as heard in the lyrics to "<a href="/wiki/Dreams_(The_Game_song)" title="Dreams (The Game song)">Dreams</a>"), but an <a href="/wiki/Injunction" title="Injunction">injunction</a> filed at the request of <a href="/wiki/Eazy-E" title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a>'s widow prevented him from using <a href="/wiki/N.W.A" title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>'s name in the album title. Thus, the album was titled <i>The Documentary</i>, which featured Dr. Dre and 50 Cent as executive producers. The album spawned the hit <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a> "<a href="/wiki/How_We_Do_(song)" title="How We Do (song)">How We Do</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Hate_It_or_Love_It" title="Hate It or Love It">Hate It or Love It</a>", the latter receiving two Grammy nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_2006_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy_2006-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was the sixteenth best selling album of 2005 in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> It also debuted at number seven in the United Kingdom and sold over five million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In October 2004, he released <i><a href="/wiki/Untold_Story_(album)" title="Untold Story (album)">Untold Story</a></i> through Get Low Recordz, which sold over 82,000 copies within its first three months.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The album featured artists like <a href="/wiki/Sean_T_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean T (rapper)">Sean T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Noble" title="Young Noble">Young Noble</a> (of the <a href="/wiki/Outlawz" title="Outlawz">Outlawz</a>), and JT the Bigga Figga.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Game also appeared on various mixtapes hosted by DJ's such as <a href="/wiki/DJ_Kayslay" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ Kayslay">DJ Kayslay</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Whoo_Kid" title="DJ Whoo Kid">DJ Whoo Kid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Clue" title="DJ Clue">DJ Clue</a>. Game also released a second mixtape <i>You Know What It Is Vol. 2</i> through his own record label and appeared on the video game <i><a href="/wiki/NBA_Live_2004" title="NBA Live 2004">NBA Live 2004</a></i> on a song produced by <a href="/wiki/Fredwreck" title="Fredwreck">Fredwreck</a> called "Can't Stop Me".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later that year, the young rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Eazy-E" title="Lil Eazy-E">Lil Eazy-E</a>, son of rapper the late <a href="/wiki/Eazy-E" title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a>, entered a feud with Game. The two used to be close associates and recorded music together. Lil' Eazy-E has since directed numerous diss songs targeting the rapper and has expressed his anger over what he felt was Game's misuse of his father's name. Game responded by claiming that Lil' Eazy-E was trying to establish himself off the success he had made since releasing <i>The Documentary</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He released a song titled "120 Bars" where he claimed that Lil' Eazy-E does not write his own lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> However, on the same track, Game stated that he would rather not feud with Lil' Eazy-E due to the deep respect he has for Lil' Eazy-E's father. Lil' Eazy-E later responded with "They Know Me". On October 30, 2006, Game went on <a href="/wiki/KDAY" title="KDAY">KDAY</a> and said that he and Lil' Eazy-E had ended their feud.
</p><p>Dr. Dre's nemesis, <a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight" title="Suge Knight">Suge Knight</a>, also had an ongoing feud with Game that stemmed from Yukmouth's claim that Game had been slapped by Suge Knight. Game responded on his website, saying that if Suge Knight had ever touched him, he would be "six feet under".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> After the 2005 <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a> show, associates of <a href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records" title="Death Row Records">Death Row Records</a> had their invitations to a party hosted by <a href="/wiki/Ciara" title="Ciara">Ciara</a> rescinded. Supposedly, a member of Death Row Records tried to steal Game's chain. Game stated on his website that he disliked Suge Knight because of "the lives he has endangered". In <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> for the 2005 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, Suge Knight was shot and wounded at <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s party by an unknown gunman.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Game vigorously denied involvement in the shooting, but the incident renewed efforts to pacify hip hop feuds and Game has consequently been discouraged from attending certain events in hopes of averting retaliation.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Later, Game and various representatives of California's rap cliques formed a West Coast "peace treaty" to end many rivalries between West Coast rappers.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Although Suge Knight did not attend, he and Game declared their feud over.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Doctor.27s_Advocate_and_feud_with_G-Unit_.282005.E2.80.932007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Doctor's_Advocate_and_feud_with_G-Unit_(2005–2007)"><i>Doctor's Advocate</i> and feud with G-Unit (2005–2007)</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:TheGameApr2011.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TheGameApr2011.jpg/220px-TheGameApr2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="272" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TheGameApr2011.jpg/330px-TheGameApr2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/TheGameApr2011.jpg/440px-TheGameApr2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3207" /></a><figcaption>Game performing at Supafest 2011</figcaption></figure>
<p>In early 2005, Game entered a feud with G-Unit. Even before Game's major label debut was released and their feud became public, there was tension between Game and 50 Cent.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Soon after <i>The Documentary'</i>s release, 50 Cent talked about an accident that occurred in the <a href="/wiki/Strip_club" title="Strip club">strip club</a> by stating that he felt that the rapper's actions of not partnering with <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> to react to <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a> after the <a href="/wiki/New_York_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="New York (Ja Rule song)">New York</a> song written by <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a> were wrong and then booted Game out of <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>. 50 Cent also claimed that he was not getting his proper credit for the creation of the album, as he had written six of the songs, all of which Game denied. During that dispute, a member of Game's entourage was shot during a confrontation that occurred at the <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a> studio in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-Beef_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beef-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> After the situation between them escalated, 50 Cent and Game held a press conference to announce their reconciliation.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Fans had mixed feelings as to whether the rappers created a publicity stunt to boost the sales of the two albums the pair had just released.<sup id="cite_ref-Beef_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beef-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, even after the situation had apparently deflated,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> G-Unit continued to feud with Game, denouncing his street credibility in the media and claimed that, without their support, he would not score a hit if he made a second album. Game responded during a performance at <a href="/wiki/Summer_Jam_(festival)" title="Summer Jam (festival)">Summer Jam</a> and launched a boycott of G-Unit called "G-Unot".<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the performance at Summer Jam, Game responded with a song titled "300 Barz and Running'", an extended "diss" aimed at G-Unit as well as members of <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella Records</a> on the mixtape <i>You Know What It Is Vol. 3</i>. The track is unique in that it is nearly 14 minutes long, in which Game criticizes all members of G-Unit, amongst many others. 50 Cent responded through his "<a href="/wiki/Piggy_Bank_(song)" title="Piggy Bank (song)">Piggy Bank</a>" music video, which features Game as a <a href="/wiki/Mr._Potato_Head" title="Mr. Potato Head">Mr. Potato Head</a> doll and also parodies other rivals.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Since then, both groups continued to attack each other. Game released two more mixtapes, <i>Ghost Unit</i> and a mixtape/DVD called <i><a href="/wiki/Stop_Snitchin,_Stop_Lyin" title="Stop Snitchin, Stop Lyin">Stop Snitchin, Stop Lyin</a></i>. 50 Cent's rebuttal was "Not Rich, Still Lyin'" where he mocks Game.<sup id="cite_ref-240Bars_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240Bars-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In addition, G-Unit started to respond on numerous mixtapes and then-new G-Unit member <a href="/wiki/Spider_Loc" title="Spider Loc">Spider Loc</a> began dissing Game. Game responded with "240 Bars (Spider Joke)",<sup id="cite_ref-240Bars_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240Bars-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> a song mainly aimed at Spider Loc, but also addressing <a href="/wiki/Tony_Yayo" title="Tony Yayo">Tony Yayo</a> and rap group <a href="/wiki/M.O.P." title="M.O.P.">M.O.P.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-240Bars_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240Bars-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and on the song "The Funeral 100 Bars".
</p><p>The feud between Game and <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella Records</a> grew out of an earlier rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Memphis_Bleek" title="Memphis Bleek">Memphis Bleek</a> over the name of his label (<a href="/wiki/Get_Low_Records" title="Get Low Records">Get Low Records</a>), which was similar to the one Game was previously signed to (<a href="/wiki/Get_Low_Recordz" title="Get Low Recordz">Get Low Recordz</a>). On the single "<a href="/wiki/Westside_Story_(song)" title="Westside Story (song)">Westside Story</a>", Game raps that "I don't do button-up shirts or drive <a href="/wiki/Maybach" title="Maybach">Maybachs</a>", which was perceived as being directed towards <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, though Game stated it was directed toward <a href="/wiki/Ja_Rule" title="Ja Rule">Ja Rule</a>. Later Jay-Z performed a freestyle on <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a>'s radio show on Hot 97 and in it, he repeatedly used the word <i>game</i>, which some hip hop fans<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (July 2017)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> believed was directed towards Game. Game responded with "My Bitch" in which the first verse is directed at <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, the second verse is directed at <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and the third verse at <a href="/wiki/Suge_Knight" title="Suge Knight">Suge Knight</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg/220px-The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg/330px-The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg/440px-The_Game_-_Hip_Hop_Jam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>Game performing at the 2007 Hip Hop Jam festival in the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Due to his disputes with 50 Cent, Game left <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a> and signed with <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a> another label under <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Interscope-Geffen-A%26M" class="mw-redirect" title="Interscope-Geffen-A&amp;M">Interscope-Geffen-A&amp;M</a> division to terminate his contractual obligations with G-Unit in the summer of 2006. The rapper's second major-label album <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor%27s_Advocate" title="Doctor&#39;s Advocate">Doctor's Advocate</a></i> was released on November 14, 2006. This album was set out by Game to prove that he was still able to make good music and be a successful artist without the help of Dr. Dre or 50 Cent. While Game originally claimed Dr. Dre would still do production on the album in the November issue of <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i> magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> he admitted in September after the <i>XXL</i> interview was conducted during an interview on radio station <a href="/wiki/Power_105" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 105">Power 105</a> that Dr. Dre would not be producing any tracks<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> although four previously unreleased tracks produced by Dr. Dre were released on the Internet, but no reason was given as to why they were not included on the album. The album debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, selling over 358,000 copies its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2006, Game extended a peace treaty to 50 Cent, which was not immediately replied to.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> However, a couple days later on <a href="/wiki/Power_106" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 106">Power 106</a>, he stated that the treaty was only offered for one day. On Game's album <i>Doctor's Advocate</i>, he says the feud is over on a few of the songs. The feud seemed to have gained steam after Tony Yayo allegedly slapped the fourteen-year-old son of <a href="/wiki/Czar_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Czar Entertainment">Czar Entertainment</a> CEO Jimmy Rosemond. Game responded with "Body Bags" on <i>You Know What It Is Vol. 4</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
Since Young Buck was dismissed from G-Unit by 50 Cent, there have been interviews from both Game and Young Buck stating they never had a problem with each other. In an interview Young Buck said he was aware of Game's support and that Lloyd Banks and Tony Yayo did not reach out to him.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="LAX_and_The_R.E.D._Album_.282007.E2.80.932012.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="LAX_and_The_R.E.D._Album_(2007–2012)"><i>LAX</i> and <i>The R.E.D. Album</i> (2007–2012)</span></h3>
<p>Game appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park</a></i> on May 16, where he confirmed <i><a href="/wiki/LAX_(album)" title="LAX (album)">LAX</a></i> would be the last studio album he records. He had originally announced that <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> would be producing for the album, but neither Dr. Dre nor Aftermath Entertainment had confirmed. The album went head to head with <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Slipknot_(band)" title="Slipknot (band)">Slipknot</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/All_Hope_Is_Gone" title="All Hope Is Gone">All Hope Is Gone</a></i> on the <i>Billboard</i>&#160;200 albums chart, seeing that both albums were released on August 22, 2008, therefore both albums were competing for the number one spot on the <i>Billboard</i>&#160;200. <i>LAX</i> ended up debuting at number two on the <i>Billboard</i>&#160;200, at first, it looked like <i>LAX</i> had debuted ahead of <i>All Hope Is Gone</i> by 13 copies. Initially, <i>Billboard</i> published an article stating that the Game had secured the top spot with a margin of 13&#160;units, in what was described as the "closest race for number one since <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" class="mw-redirect" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> began tracking Data in 1991".<sup id="cite_ref-MusicWeek_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MusicWeek-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Slipknot's labels <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roadrunner_Records" title="Roadrunner Records">Roadrunner Records</a> asked for a SoundScan recount, a historic first. Nielsen proceeded to the recount, which placed <i>LAX</i> at number two with 238,382 copies, and Slipknot in the first position with 239,516 copies scanned, a margin of 1,134 copies. After the recount 12&#160;hours later, the article was rewritten and Slipknot was awarded the number one spot.<sup id="cite_ref-MusicWeek_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MusicWeek-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <i>LAX</i> spawned four singles: "<a href="/wiki/Game%27s_Pain" title="Game&#39;s Pain">Game's Pain</a>" with R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Keyshia_Cole" title="Keyshia Cole">Keyshia Cole</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Dope_Boys" title="Dope Boys">Dope Boys</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Blink-182" title="Blink-182">Blink-182</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Travis_Barker" title="Travis Barker">Travis Barker</a>, "<a href="/wiki/My_Life_(The_Game_song)" title="My Life (The Game song)">My Life</a>" with rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Camera_Phone_(song)" title="Camera Phone (song)">Camera Phone</a>" with R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>. In the United States, the album has sold over 660,100 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was confirmed in May 2009, that Game began working on a new album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_R.E.D._Album" title="The R.E.D. Album">The R.E.D. Album</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On June 26, 2009, Game released a song titled "<a href="/wiki/Better_on_the_Other_Side" title="Better on the Other Side">Better on the Other Side</a>" a <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> tribute, the day after Jackson's death. It features <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Diddy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Winans" title="Mario Winans">Mario Winans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Brown (American entertainer)">Chris Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Game_(rapper)-LAX/The_R.E.D._Album_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Game_(rapper)-LAX/The_R.E.D._Album-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On October 3, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> posted a picture on his Twitter of himself, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> and Game in the studio working together,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The picture was taken a day earlier and it marked the first time Game had worked with Dr. Dre for some years since the beef with former fellow <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a> labelmate <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> caused him to release his two following albums on <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a>. Later in early January 2010 Game posted a twitpic of him wearing a lot of Aftermath chains with a caption saying "It's funny how things come Full Circle". Later he confirmed that he had returned to <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath Entertainment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gameofficiallyreturns_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gameofficiallyreturns-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He traveled to <a href="/wiki/Prishtin%C3%AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Prishtinë">Prishtinë</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> for a concert, that according to him would be the greatest of his life. In an interview there, Game stated: "I love Albanians, If I could be reborn, I'd be reborn Albanian".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On June 3, 2011, <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" class="mw-redirect" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a> announced that Game was working with <a href="/wiki/Odd_Future" title="Odd Future">Odd Future</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_The_Creator" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyler, The Creator">Tyler, The Creator</a> on a track called "Martians vs. Goblins".<sup id="cite_ref-Pitchfork:_Tyler_the_Creator_Working_With_the_Game_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork:_Tyler_the_Creator_Working_With_the_Game-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Finally released on August 23, 2011, <i>The R.E.D. Album</i> reached number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with first-week sales of 98,000 units.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Jesus_Piece_and_OKE_.282012.E2.80.932013.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jesus_Piece_and_OKE_(2012–2013)"><i>Jesus Piece</i> and <i>OKE</i> (2012–2013)</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Piece_(album)" title="Jesus Piece (album)">Jesus Piece (album)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Kill_Everything" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Kill Everything">Operation Kill Everything</a></div>
<p>Shortly after the release of the long-delayed eighth studio album, Game announced he had begun work on his ninth album. At the time titled <i>Soundtrack to Chaos</i>, he said the album would not feature him "name-dropping" or feature any artists as guests for vocals.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In March 2012, Game announced the album name had been changed to <i>F.I.V.E.: Fear Is Victory's Evolution</i> and that it could be his last album released under Interscope,<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx1_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx1-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> but on August 28 the rapper published a new title: <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus_Piece_(album)" title="Jesus Piece (album)">Jesus Piece</a></i>.
</p><p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> on November 8, Game revealed that as <i>Jesus Piece</i> is his last album before his deal with Interscope comes to a close, he has had talks with both <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records" title="Cash Money Records">Cash Money Records</a> for a possible new record deal. He also stated that he would consider releasing music independently.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Game_Supafest_(5605987500).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/The_Game_Supafest_%285605987500%29.jpg/220px-The_Game_Supafest_%285605987500%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/The_Game_Supafest_%285605987500%29.jpg/330px-The_Game_Supafest_%285605987500%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/The_Game_Supafest_%285605987500%29.jpg/440px-The_Game_Supafest_%285605987500%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a><figcaption>The Game performing in 2011</figcaption></figure>
<p>The album was released on December 11, 2012, with features from <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Foxx" title="Jamie Foxx">Jamie Foxx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyga" title="Tyga">Tyga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Brown (American entertainer)">Chris Brown</a> among others. In promotion for the album Game started a free weekly music giveaway titled "Sunday Service". All the tracks are leftovers from <i>Jesus Piece</i>. Game also showed interest in making a future collaboration LP with Chris Brown.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Game explained the concept of <i>Jesus Piece</i> does not have a spiritual theme, but it would have a "Gangster" theme of enjoying life while also having faith in God.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <i>Jesus Piece</i> became Game's first album since the multi-platinum selling and critically acclaimed <i>The Documentary</i>, to feature production from <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>. Game announced on social media that every Sunday leading up to the album that he would be dropping new music, which failed to make the album's final cut. Game compared the album's quality of production and high number of guests to his mentor <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronic_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="The Chronic 2001">The Chronic 2001</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Upon release the album received generally positive reviews by <a href="/wiki/Music_critic" class="mw-redirect" title="Music critic">music critics</a>. Most reviewers have praised the production and guests and the album.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <i>Jesus Piece</i> debuted at number six on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with first-week sales of 86,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> As of July 26, 2013, it has sold 281,000 copies according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" class="mw-redirect" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 30, 2012, Game announced that he and fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Stat_Quo" title="Stat Quo">Stat Quo</a> were starting a new record label titled Rolex Records. Both artists would use the label to release new music and sign other artists.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On October 1, 2013, Game announced he was officially leaving Interscope Records, and that he was now a free agent.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The following day he told <a href="/wiki/Artistdirect" title="Artistdirect">Artistdirect</a> that him signing to <a href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records" title="Cash Money Records">Cash Money Records</a> was likely, and that a final announcement of a signing would probably come in January 2014. He also stated he had talked to Kendrick Lamar, <a href="/wiki/Nipsey_Hussle" title="Nipsey Hussle">Nipsey Hussle</a>, and Snoop Dogg about possibly doing collaboration albums in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 8, the Game released his first project since leaving Interscope, a mixtape titled <i><a href="/wiki/Operation_Kill_Everything" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Kill Everything">Operation Kill Everything</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape featured guest appearances by <a href="/wiki/Too_Short" title="Too Short">Too Short</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schoolboy_Q" title="Schoolboy Q">Schoolboy Q</a>, Chris Brown, Lil Wayne, <a href="/wiki/Problem_(rapper)" title="Problem (rapper)">Problem</a>, Nipsey Hussle, <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>, Stat Quo, and <a href="/wiki/Ty$" class="mw-redirect" title="Ty$">Ty$</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The day after the mixtape's release, the Game spoke to <i>XXL</i> where he said, he had begun working on his ninth studio album, which will be executive produced by Cool &amp; Dre. He mentioned he had also talked to <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> about a record deal, and was still possible that he would re-sign with Interscope.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Then the following day, the Game released a deluxe edition of <i>OKE</i> to iTunes, featuring two bonus tracks, including "Hollywood" a song with Scarface.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="The_Documentary_2.2C_1992_and_feud_with_Meek_Mill_.282013.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Documentary_2,_1992_and_feud_with_Meek_Mill_(2013–2018)"><i>The Documentary 2</i>, <i>1992</i> and feud with Meek Mill (2013–2018)</span></h3>
<p>On October 12, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">Birdman</a> announced that he had signed the Game to Cash Money Records, which Game later seemingly confirmed that same day.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On December 11, 2013, Game stated that he was not officially signed to <a href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records" title="Cash Money Records">Cash Money Records</a> stating "It's just trying to figure out what's the best for Cash Money, what's the best for Game at this point in his career. That's pretty much family and that's where I'm at, at this point", he said. "Nothing's written in stone, but that's where I'm leaning."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 16, 2014, the Game released the compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_Moon:_Year_of_the_Wolf" title="Blood Moon: Year of the Wolf">Blood Moon: Year of the Wolf</a>'</i>s first single "Bigger than Me".<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The song heavily samples rock group <a href="/wiki/Poli%C3%A7a" title="Poliça">Poliça</a>'s 2013 single "Warrior Lord". The following day, the Game announced that his sixth studio album, a sequel to his debut album <i>The Documentary</i>, would be arriving in January 2015, with <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> returning as producer along with <a href="/wiki/Just_Blaze" title="Just Blaze">Just Blaze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> He also expressed interest in getting Nicki Minaj featured on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The second single from <i>Year of the Wolf</i>, titled "<a href="/wiki/Or_Nah_(The_Game_song)" title="Or Nah (The Game song)">Or Nah</a>" was released on July 1, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 18, 2015, the Game announced that <i><a href="/wiki/The_Documentary_2" title="The Documentary 2">The Documentary 2</a></i> would be released June 30, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The album was pushed back to August 7.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On June 23, Game released the first single, titled "<a href="/wiki/100_(The_Game_song)" title="100 (The Game song)">100</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>. Target began displaying the original artwork for <i>The Documentary 2</i> July 13, 2015. However, the release date was pushed back again, to August 28, then eventually to October 9.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A week later on October 16, Game released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Documentary_2.5" title="The Documentary 2.5">The Documentary 2.5</a></i> the second half of <i>The Documentary 2</i>.
</p><p>The Game and <a href="/wiki/Skrillex" title="Skrillex">Skrillex</a> collaborated on a song named "<a href="/wiki/El_Chapo_(song)" title="El Chapo (song)">El Chapo</a>", which was released on October 9, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 1, 2016, the Game ended his twelve-year feud with 50 Cent when the two were in the Ace of Diamonds Strip Club and he said "What happened, that shit was 12 years ago."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 16, 2016, the Game released "92 Bars", a five-minute freestyle, used to promote his upcoming seventh studio album, but was also rumored to have been a diss towards rapper <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Previously, Mill and Game collaborated on 2015's "The Soundtrack".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Hours after the release of "92 Bars", Game admitted that the freestyle was specifically a diss towards Mill. The next day, the two rappers ended up in an <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> exchange, with the Game cyber-flirting with Meek Mill's girlfriend, <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, as well as accusing him of calling the police, informing the authorities about a robbery involving <a href="/wiki/Sean_Kingston" title="Sean Kingston">Sean Kingston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On September 18, Meek Mill released a diss track towards Game, a remix to <a href="/wiki/Young_M.A." class="mw-redirect" title="Young M.A.">Young M.A.</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Ooouuu" title="Ooouuu">Ooouuu</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Omelly" class="mw-redirect" title="Omelly">Omelly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Sigel" title="Beanie Sigel">Beanie Sigel</a>. Two days later, the Game responded with "Pest Control", using the same beat and sending shots at Meek Mill, Omelly, Beanie Sigel and Sean Kingston.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 the two reconciled after Mill's incarceration and subsequent release from prison. On October 27, 2017, the Game released the single "Oh I" featuring <a href="/wiki/Jeremih" title="Jeremih">Jeremih</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Thug" title="Young Thug">Young Thug</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevyn_Streeter" title="Sevyn Streeter">Sevyn Streeter</a>.
</p><p>From his <i><a href="/wiki/1992_(album)" title="1992 (album)">1992</a></i> album, he released "True Colors/It's On", "All Eyez", "What Your Life Like", and "Baby You" featuring <a href="/wiki/Jason_Derulo" title="Jason Derulo">Jason Derulo</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Born_2_Rap_.282019-21.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Born_2_Rap_(2019-21)"><i>Born 2 Rap</i> (2019-21)</span></h3>
<p>In December 2016, the Game announced that he is working on his next and final album.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On June 21, 2019, he released the first single of the album titled "West Side". On November 1, 2019, the Game released the second single, "Stainless", featuring <a href="/wiki/Anderson_.Paak" title="Anderson .Paak">Anderson .Paak</a>. His ninth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Born_2_Rap" title="Born 2 Rap">Born 2 Rap</a></i> was released on November 29, 2019, his fifiteth birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number nineteen on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.
</p>
<h3><span id="Drillmatic_.E2.80.93_Heart_vs._Mind_and_feud_with_Eminem_.282021.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Drillmatic_–_Heart_vs._Mind_and_feud_with_Eminem_(2021–present)"><i>Drillmatic – Heart vs. Mind</i> and feud with Eminem (2021–present)</span></h3>
<p>In November 2020, The Game returned with the Lil Wayne-assisted "A.I. with the Braids", his first single since <i>Born 2 Rap</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewProject_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewProject-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In January 2021, The Game's manager, Wack 100, said to <a href="/wiki/AllHipHop" title="AllHipHop">AllHipHop</a> that although Game called <i>Born 2 Rap</i> his final album and showed interest in managing and signing artists during retirement, he is however is back in the studio working on a new project, tentatively titled <i>30 for 30</i>. No further details have been announced.<sup id="cite_ref-NewProject_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewProject-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2022, the Game's feud with 50 Cent reignited after the latter critiqued Game's <i>Drink Champs</i> interview with <a href="/wiki/N.O.R.E." title="N.O.R.E.">N.O.R.E.</a>, where he claimed that 50's former record sale competitor <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> did "more for me in two weeks than [Dr.] Dre did for me throughout my entire career".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The Game responded, commenting that he enclosed the entirety of G-Unit as a group and <a href="/wiki/G-Unit_Clothing_Company" title="G-Unit Clothing Company">clothing brand</a> "in a casket", also expressing his likeliness in the <a href="/wiki/Power_(TV_series)" title="Power (TV series)"><i>Power</i></a> television trilogy (which 50 Cent co-produces), but warning him to "leave [the past] alone or else... I'm outside #Numinati".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Then, two months later, in March, 50 Cent published a video via Instagram of Game being shunned by former Interscope Records CEO <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a> at a basketball game, poking fun of it while also commenting "50 wrote ya hits". The Game once again flamed 50 after the claims were brought back up and also bragged to "get [50's] girlfriend out of my DM's".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> This was believed to have been a consequential result of Game claiming on <i>Drink Champs</i> to be "the best and a better rapper" than former Aftermath labelmate <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, with whom 50 still remains close friends.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Game's manager, Wack 100, has subliminally called out or questioned 50 Cent's credibility, over the rapper's surprise appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVI" title="Super Bowl LVI">Super Bowl LVI</a> halftime show and ghostwriting allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 15, the Game announced his eleventh album, <i><a href="/wiki/Drillmatic_%E2%80%93_Heart_vs._Mind" title="Drillmatic – Heart vs. Mind">Drillmatic – Heart vs. Mind</a></i>, revealing the cover art and the release date. The album was released on August 12, 2022. The album is executive produced by Hit-Boy, Kanye West, Wack 100 and others.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The album included guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Chloe_Bailey" title="Chloe Bailey">Chloe Bailey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Rocky" title="ASAP Rocky">ASAP Rocky</a>, former rival Meek Mill, <a href="/wiki/YoungBoy_Never_Broke_Again" title="YoungBoy Never Broke Again">YoungBoy Never Broke Again</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a>, <a href="/wiki/YG_(rapper)" title="YG (rapper)">YG</a> and twenty-two others throughout its 30-track listing; it also includes the Kanye West duet, "<a href="/wiki/Eazy_(song)" title="Eazy (song)">Eazy</a>", which samples the <a href="/wiki/Eazy-E" title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a> 1988 title track, "<a href="/wiki/Eazy-Duz-It_(song)" title="Eazy-Duz-It (song)">Eazy-Duz-It</a>", as well as "The Black Slim Shady", which is a ten-minute diss towards Eminem.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Selling 25,000 equivalent units in the first week, it debuted at number twelve on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, becoming Game's lowest-selling album in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h2>
<p>In 2000, the Game appeared on the dating television show <i><a href="/wiki/Change_of_Heart_(TV_series)" title="Change of Heart (TV series)">Change of Heart</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> in the segment his partner criticized him for "acting macho when in reality is said to be sensitive." The episode came to an end where a mutual friend of the Game and his partner suggested in them staying together, the Game decided to stay together but was rebuffed by the offer when his partner agreed to a change of heart and the Game was subsequently dumped on TV.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Game also ventured into acting. In 2004, he had a minor role voicing the character "<a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_Grand_Theft_Auto:_San_Andreas#Mark_&quot;B_Dup&quot;_Wayne" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas">B-Dup</a>" in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_San_Andreas" title="Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas">Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas</a></i>. He also voiced himself in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Def_Jam:_Icon" title="Def Jam: Icon">Def Jam: Icon</a></i>. In 2006, he made his film debut in <i><a href="/wiki/Waist_Deep" title="Waist Deep">Waist Deep</a></i> as a character named "Big Meat" and is currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2017)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> filming two more movies.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (May 2018)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Game was chosen to play and bought a large amount of shares for the <a href="/wiki/Inglewood_Cobras" title="Inglewood Cobras">Inglewood Cobras</a>, established in 2005 and playing in the <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(2000-present)" class="mw-redirect" title="American Basketball Association (2000-present)">American Basketball Association</a> basketball franchise team.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The team folded after playing fewer than five games in the ABA in the league's 2005–2006 season. The team was coached by former <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a> player <a href="/wiki/Sean_Higgins_(basketball)" title="Sean Higgins (basketball)">Sean Higgins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Game has also partnered with <a href="/wiki/310_Motoring" title="310 Motoring">310 Motoring</a> to create his own shoe, The Hurricanes. A portion of the proceeds of the shoe were donated to the victims of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012–2013, he promoted his <i>60 Days of Fitness</i> challenge, a rigorous fitness and nutrition regime with his brother and trainer Byrd.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Game has, on several occasions, honored the memory of those who died during the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian genocide</a> and has expressed his sympathy towards the events.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The Game is also an avid supporter of <a href="/wiki/Black_Lives_Matter" title="Black Lives Matter">Black Lives Matter</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Record_labels">Record labels</span></h3>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Wall_Street_Records" title="The Black Wall Street Records">The Black Wall Street Records</a></b> was an American independent record label founded in 2002, by the Game.
</p><p><b>Blood Money Entertainment</b> was an American independent <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record label</a>. In December 2012, the Game founded a new record label, Rolex Records, alongside fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Stat_Quo" title="Stat Quo">Stat Quo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Following its founding, he bought his entire team at the record label <a href="/wiki/Rolex_watch" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolex watch">Rolex watches</a>. After a six-month legal battle with <a href="/wiki/Rolex" title="Rolex">Rolex</a>, he changed the name and logo of the record label to The Firm,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> which then became Blood Money Entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The label has signed West Coast rappers <a href="/wiki/Skeme" title="Skeme">Skeme</a>, King Marie, Pharaoh Jackson and Dubb.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Prolific Records</b> was an American independent record label founded by the Game in the autumn of 2019. According to court documents obtained by AllHipHop, Priscilla Rainey was granted ownership of the Game's <a href="/wiki/Vanity_label" title="Vanity label">vanity label</a>, as well as royalties from his tenth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Born_2_Rap" title="Born 2 Rap">Born 2 Rap</a></i> (2019). This means Rainey now has full control over any salary the Game was receiving through his imprint.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>100 Entertainment</b> is an American independent record label founded in 2021 by the Game and his manager, Wack 100.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Taylor is the father of two sons and one daughter.
</p><p>Taylor announced that he was engaged to actress and model Valeisha Butterfield, the daughter of U.S. Congressman <a href="/wiki/G._K._Butterfield" title="G. K. Butterfield">G. K. Butterfield</a>. The couple were set to marry in March 2007, but the engagement was called off in June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the couple broke off their engagement, Taylor became involved in a relationship with Tiffney Cambridge, a sixth-grade teacher. <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> broadcast two seasons of <i>Marrying the Game</i>, a reality television series about the Game and Cambridge, as they prepared to walk down the aisle. The relationship was "love at first sight" when Cambridge met Jayceon. Despite reservations regarding Taylor's career, the relationship lasted eight years, but no marriage plans materialized despite the series.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Cambridge accused Taylor of physical abuse throughout the relationship, which he denied.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_case_of_fan_assault">2005 case of fan assault</span></h3>
<p>Game, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound" title="Tha Dogg Pound">Tha Dogg Pound</a>, were <a href="/wiki/Civil_lawsuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil lawsuit">sued</a> for assaulting a fan on stage at a May 2005 concert at the <a href="/wiki/White_River_Amphitheatre" title="White River Amphitheatre">White River Amphitheatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Auburn,_Washington" title="Auburn, Washington">Auburn, Washington</a>. The accuser, Richard Monroe Jr., claimed he was beaten by the artists' entourage while mounting the stage.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> He alleged that he reacted to an "open invite" to come on stage. Before he could, Snoop's bodyguards grabbed him and he was beaten unconscious by crewmembers, including the rapper and producer <a href="/wiki/Soopafly" title="Soopafly">Soopafly</a>; Snoop and Game were included in the suit for not intervening. The lawsuit focuses on a pecuniary claim of $22&#160;million in punitive and <a href="/wiki/Compensatory_damages" class="mw-redirect" title="Compensatory damages">compensatory damages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battery_(tort)" title="Battery (tort)">battery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Negligence" title="Negligence">negligence</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intentional_infliction_of_emotional_distress" title="Intentional infliction of emotional distress">intentional infliction of emotional distress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The concerned parties appeared in court in April 2009.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (July 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_case_of_disorderly_conduct">2005 case of disorderly conduct</span></h3>
<p>On October 28, 2005, Game was charged with <a href="/wiki/Disorderly_conduct" title="Disorderly conduct">disorderly conduct</a> and resisting arrest in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>. At one point, police said his companions were <a href="/wiki/Pepper_spray" title="Pepper spray">pepper sprayed</a> when they surrounded officers in a threatening manner.<sup id="cite_ref-NorthCarolinaIncident_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorthCarolinaIncident-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Mall security officers said the rapper was wearing a full-face <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> mask, filming shoppers, cursed loudly, and refused to leave when asked. Game continued to act up and was arrested, a police statement said. Game claimed that officers overreacted and that he did nothing wrong when he was pepper-sprayed by the mall security.<sup id="cite_ref-NorthCarolinaIncident_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorthCarolinaIncident-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The five officers involved in the incident ended up suing Game for <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">defamation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The officers were awarded $5 million in compensatory damages, which was upheld on appeal by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Court_of_Appeals" title="North Carolina Court of Appeals">North Carolina Court of Appeals</a> in February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_trial_on_assault_and_weapons_charges">2007 trial on assault and weapons charges</span></h3>
<p>On May 11, 2007, Game was arrested at his home, reportedly in connection with an incident at a basketball game in <a href="/wiki/South_Los_Angeles" title="South Los Angeles">South Los Angeles</a> in February 2007. He is alleged to have threatened a person with a gun. The arrest took place after his home was searched for three hours. Game was released early the next day after posting $50,000 bail.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On January 9, 2008, a Los Angeles judge scheduled February 4 as the beginning date for Game's trial on assault and weapons charges.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> After pleading <a href="/wiki/Nolo_contendere" title="Nolo contendere">no contest</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">felony</a> weapons charge on February 11, Game was sentenced to 60 days in jail, 150 hours of community service, and three years of <a href="/wiki/Probation" title="Probation">probation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_controversies">2011 controversies</span></h3>
<p>In 2011, Game was refused entry to Canada for alleged gang ties in Los Angeles; concert organisers said he was associated with the <a href="/wiki/Bloods_(gang)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloods (gang)">Bloods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 12, 2011, the Game decided to tweet his search for a supposed internship opening. In the message sent to his over 580,000 followers, he posted the number to call as the emergency line for the Los Angeles Sheriff's Department. The Game's fans jammed the line for hours. Initially, the Game denied any wrongdoing, saying the tweet was "a mistake". The Game then posted a message saying the sheriff's department can "track a tweet down but you can't solve murders!" A criminal investigation was launched stating that the Game could be charged for obstruction of justice. Despite all of this, the Los Angeles Sheriff's Department issued this statement: "Based upon our investigation, as well as consultation with the Los Angeles County District Attorney's Office, the LASD considers the criminal investigation into this matter closed. The Los Angeles County Sheriff's Department will not be seeking criminal charges." The Game issued an apology on CNN saying, "My sincerest apologies to the Sheriff's Department, it was a joke gone wrong."
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_physical_altercation_with_40_Glocc">2012 physical altercation with 40 Glocc</span></h3>
<p>On July 8, 2012, <a href="/wiki/40_Glocc" title="40 Glocc">40 Glocc</a> got into an altercation with the Game. In a video clip, allegedly shot by the Game via Game's iPhone during the fight, 40 Glocc is seen running into a bush after being beaten up by the fellow West Coast rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Game defended what he did by saying he was retaliating for Glocc going up to rappers <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plies_(rapper)" title="Plies (rapper)">Plies</a> in the past with large entourages.<sup id="cite_ref-www.hiphopdx.com_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.hiphopdx.com-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In October 2012, 40 Glocc filed a lawsuit for $4.54 million for <a href="/wiki/Assault" title="Assault">assault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battery_(crime)" title="Battery (crime)">battery</a>, as well as damaging his reputation. This included $500,000 in pain and suffering; $500,000 in emotional distress; $750,000 in lost earnings; $2 million for punitive damages; $25,000 in medical expenses; and various other reasons. Since then, Glocc has gone on a smear campaign against the Game, releasing his diss "The Full Edit" in December 2012. Game has similarly addressed the situation in several interviews, claiming that filing a lawsuit of this nature "disintegrates your street cred".<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, 40 Glocc assaulted Game's manager Dontay "Taydoe" Kidd in Las Vegas, Nevada.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Glocc won the lawsuit and was awarded $3000.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_sexual_assault_case">2016 sexual assault case</span></h3>
<p>In 2016, a judge ruled that the Game was liable for sexually assaulting Priscilla Rainey, then a contestant on <i><a href="/wiki/She%27s_Got_Game" title="She&#39;s Got Game">She Got Game</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> reality show starring the Game.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Rainey claimed she had agreed to go on a date with the Game, believing it would be on camera; however, when she met the rapper at a Chicago restaurant, there was allegedly no production&#160;crew.&#160;The lawsuit further alleged&#160;the Game showed up to the date "highly intoxicated on alcohol and drugs (which was typical), and sexually assaulted the plaintiff [Rainey] on several occasions that night. This included him forcefully reaching his hand inside her dress to rub her bare vagina and buttocks".<sup id="cite_ref-Complex_Seize_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex_Seize-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2019, an appellate court affirmed the entire $7.1 million judgment.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> However, according to Rainey, the rapper&#160;failed to paid her any money in the years since she received the judgement. Rainey subsequently filed a <a href="/wiki/Motion_(legal)" title="Motion (legal)">motion</a>, requesting the seizure of the Game's income, and in April 2020, she was granted ownership&#160;of the Game's&#160;independent record label Prolific Records, as well as <a href="/wiki/Royalty_payment" title="Royalty payment">royalties</a> from his 2019 album,&#160;<i><a href="/wiki/Born_2_Rap" title="Born 2 Rap">Born 2 Rap</a></i>. This resulted in Rainey gaining full control over any salary the Game would receive through his imprint label, which was launched in late 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Complex_Seize_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex_Seize-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In November 2019, the Game had addressed his legal battle with Rainey during an appearance on&#160;<i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <i>Everyday Struggle</i>,&#160;calling Rainey a liar, and&#160;insisted he was never&#160;going to pay her.<sup id="cite_ref-Complex_Seize_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complex_Seize-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_battery_misdemeanor">2017 battery misdemeanor</span></h3>
<p>In 2017, Game pleaded no contest to assaulting an off-duty police officer on March 29, 2015, during a basketball game at a Hollywood high school. Game, then 37, entered a no contest plea to one misdemeanor count each of criminal threats and battery, and also pleaded no contest to one felony count of grand theft, according to the Los Angeles County District Attorney's Office. He was immediately sentenced to three years of formal probation, 120 hours of community service and 26 anger management counseling sessions, and a 6-month suspended sentence.
</p><p>Game and an off-duty Los Angeles police officer were on opposing teams in a basketball game when the defendant intentionally fouled, then sucker-punched the victim who had just stolen the ball from the defendant and scored a basket. Game threatened to kill the victim once the defendant was ejected as a result of the punch, and on April 11, 2015, Game grabbed and threatened a man filming him being served with legal papers outside of his house and kept the victim's camera, according to the prosecutor.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
